<div id="review_2204431207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2204431207" />
    <a title="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore"><img alt="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560079929p2/5917681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2204431207?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" href="/user/show/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore">Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 97893806587" href="/book/show/11827808-the-secret-of-the-nagas">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2204431207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12843753138215487162">Three and a half stars again- As in the first instalment, it is the plot and the pace that keep one completely engrossed, one wants to keep reading on to see what happens. The plot is very exciting, imaginative, and interesting. But my complaint with the language in the first book continues in this one- it just seems unsuited to the setting and the time- not quite right. Of course, this isn't stopping me from moving on to the final instalment.<br/><br/>(review date 10 May 2014)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3433581737" />
    <a title="Jaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92480025-jaine"><img alt="Jaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581295684p2/92480025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3433581737?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaine" href="/user/show/92480025-jaine">Jaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3433581737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9705715132915118928"><strong>Everyone should read this!</strong><br/><br/>OMG. THIS ONE IS REALLY GOOD!<br/><br/>One thing I learn from this book is never judge anyone. Whether it be from their appearance or their life in general. Just never judge people.<br/><br/>I just love this book. Shiva's adventures are just so exciting! I love how he is so wise in planning the war with Parvateshwar and others. Their victory which I thought is great but has a meaning behind which is a much bigger picture than what the Neelkanth thought. His other adventures. The journey to</span>
  <span id="freeText9705715132915118928" style="display:none"><strong>Everyone should read this!</strong><br /><br />OMG. THIS ONE IS REALLY GOOD!<br /><br />One thing I learn from this book is never judge anyone. Whether it be from their appearance or their life in general. Just never judge people.<br /><br />I just love this book. Shiva's adventures are just so exciting! I love how he is so wise in planning the war with Parvateshwar and others. Their victory which I thought is great but has a meaning behind which is a much bigger picture than what the Neelkanth thought. His other adventures. The journey to Panchavati. Omg just so exciting.<br /><br />I love that the author has finally given light to a bunch of people. I can't name them all but it was just great. I learned to never judge anyone. Just anyone. Sati's sad story, her finding the truth, Daksha's surprising story and the secret the Nagas has kept. And omg. That secret is definitely unexpected.<br /><br />I also adore all the Neelkanth and Vasudev's conversations. I find them worth pondering. They are something I wouldn't have thought of but when I read them makes a lot of sense and I just adore the deep wisdom shown. Just great! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9705715132915118928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N+dQcid93zxSsCPk2O0aKbWCU/c521bYDjrf2z87dryQVOVxvhWjP4+DwGYfc+baz9M8c2qEPrMX3k+YpBo4tA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EEBX5XVwwt6TOMFlnLx2oPDiU53aOXrbYEMkbRJEuLG38+Lm7Bi+3U4LIudbIopTirM8GYlmErB5p7QuiWX2uQ==')})
  }

Still above is Vaikuntha, heaven, abode of God.The doorkeepers of Vaikuntha are the twins, Jaya and Vijaya, both whose names mean \'victory\'. One keeps you in Swarga; the other raises you <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText6962681197675824035\" style=\"display:none\">High above the sky stands Swarga, paradise, abode of the gods. Still above is Vaikuntha, heaven, abode of God.The doorkeepers of Vaikuntha are the twins, Jaya and Vijaya, both whose names mean \'victory\'. One keeps you in Swarga; the other raises you into Vaikuntha.In Vaikuntha there is bliss forever, in Swarga there is pleasure for only as long as you deserve. What is the difference between Jaya and Vijaya? Solve this puzzle and you will solve the mystery of the Mahabharata.In this enthralling retelling of India\'s greatest epic, the Mahabharata originally known as Jaya, Devdutt Pattanaik seamlessly weaves into a single narrative plots from the Sanskrit classic as well as its many folk and regional variants, including the Pandavani of Chhattisgarh, Gondhal of Maharashtra, Terukkuttu of Tamil Nadu and Yakshagana of Karnataka.Richly illustrated with over 250 line drawings by the author, the 108 chapters abound with little-known details such as the names of the hundred Kauravas, the worship of Draupadi as a goddess in Tamil Nadu, the stories of Astika, Madhavi, Jaimini, Aravan and Barbareek, the Mahabharata version of the Shakuntalam and the Ramayana, and the dating of the war based on astronomical data.With clarity and simplicity, the tales in this elegant volume reveal the eternal relevance of the Mahabharata, the complex and disturbing meditation on the human condition that has shaped Indian thought for over 3000 years.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6962681197675824035\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div <span id="freeTextContainer7562223445975228637">Amish is an IIM (Kolkata) educated, banker turned award-winning author. The success of his debut book, The Immortals of Meluha (Book 1 of the Shiva Trilogy), encouraged him to give up a fourteen-year-old career in financial services to focus on writing. He is passionate about history, mythology and philosophy, finding beauty and meaning in all world religions. <br/><br/>His 7 books have sold over 5 million </span>
  <span id="freeText7562223445975228637" style="display:none">Amish is an IIM (Kolkata) educated, banker turned award-winning author. The success of his debut book, The Immortals of Meluha (Book 1 of the Shiva Trilogy), encouraged him to give up a fourteen-year-old career in financial services to focus on writing. He is passionate about history, mythology and philosophy, finding beauty and meaning in all world religions. <br /><br />His 7 books have sold over 5 million copies and been translated into 19 Indian &amp; international languages. His Shiva Trilogy is the fastest-selling book series in Indian publishing history while his Ram Chandra Series is the second fastest-selling book series in Indian publishing history.<br /><br />In 2019, Amish was appointed to a diplomatic role as Director , The Nehru Centre in London, India's premier cultural centre abroad.</span>
